     <main class="content" itemprop="mainContentOfPage" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/Blog" role="main">
      <p id="breadcrumbs">
       <span xmlns:v="http://rdf.data-vocabulary.org/#">
        <span typeof="v:Breadcrumb">
         <a href="http://www.richardfarrar.com" property="v:title" rel="v:url">
          Home
         </a>
         
         <span rel="v:child" typeof="v:Breadcrumb">
          <a href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/podcasting/" property="v:title" rel="v:url">
           Podcasting
          </a>
          
          <span class="breadcrumb_last">
           Embedding Album Art in MP3 Files
          </span>
         </span>
        </span>
       </span>
      </p>
      <article class="post-55 post type-post status-publish format-standard has-post-thumbnail category-podcasting tag-album tag-art tag-id3 tag-jpeg tag-jpg tag-mp3 tag-podcast tag-tag tag-tags entry" itemprop="blogPost" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/BlogPosting">
       <header class="entry-header">
        <h1 class="entry-title" itemprop="headline">
         Embedding Album Art in MP3 Files
        </h1>
        <p class="entry-meta">
         <span class="entry-categories">
          Filed Under:
          <a href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/podcasting/" rel="category tag">
           Podcasting
          </a>
         </span>
        </p>
       </header>
       <div class="entry-content" itemprop="text">
        <p>
         <img align="left" alt="Embedding Cover art in MP3s" border="0" height="150" src="http://www.richardfarrar.com/wp-content/uploads/2008/06/mona-thumb.jpg" style="margin: 5px 20px 10px 0px; border: 0px none;" width="150"/>
        </p>
        <p>
         <strong>
          Album art can be embedded into MP3 files fairly easily using ID3 tags. However, before you start filling up all of your MP3 files with works of art, there are a few things that you should stop to
         </strong>
         <strong>
          consider first.
         </strong>
        </p>
        <p>
         While MP3 files were not originally intended to store additional
         <a href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/what-are-id3-tags-in-mp3-files/#more-54">
          metadata
         </a>
         within them, the release of the
         <a href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/what-are-id3-tags-in-mp3-files/">
          ID3 tag
         </a>
         protocol in 1996 suddenly made this a possibility. However, it wasnt until version 2 of the protocol became available that MP3 files could actually contain embedded album art.
        </p>
        <p>
         So, before you start cutting and pasting huge graphics and adding them into your collection of MP3 tracks, what do you need to consider to avert potential disaster?
        </p>
        <p>
         <span id="more-55">
         </span>
        </p>
        <h2>
         ID3 Tags and MP3 Files
        </h2>
        <p>
         A standard MP3 file only contains audio data, with no additional information about the artist or type of audio contained within it. To include such extra information in an MP3 track,
         <strong>
          tag data
         </strong>
         is usually added to the beginning or end of the audio file in
         <a href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/what-are-id3-tags-in-mp3-files/">
          ID3 format
         </a>
         .
        </p>
        <p>
         ID3 tags allow you to store additional information within your MP3 files such as the track title, artist name and even
         <strong>
          album art
         </strong>
         . If youre not familiar with ID3 tags, you may find my previous article on
         <a href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/what-are-id3-tags-in-mp3-files/">
          What are ID3 tags in MP3 files?
         </a>
         helpful.
        </p>
        <h2>
         Image Types
        </h2>
        <p>
         While the
         <a href="http://www.id3.org/id3v2.3.0" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-article', 'http://www.id3.org/id3v2.3.0', 'ID3v2');" target="_blank">
          ID3v2
         </a>
         tag standard allows any type of image to be embedded in an MP3 file, it does advise that either
         <acronym title="Portable Network Graphics">
          PNG
         </acronym>
         or
         <acronym title="Joint Photographic Experts Group">
          JPEG
         </acronym>
         formats should be used when interoperability with playback devices is required. Practically speaking
         <strong>
          JPEG
         </strong>
         images have been adopted as the
         <em>
          de facto
         </em>
         standard in this respect.
        </p>
        <p>
         The ID3 standard is very flexible with regards to the type and number of images that can be embedded in a MP3 single file. The full list of different images that can be embedded are:
        </p>
        <ul>
         <li>
          $00  Other
         </li>
         <li>
          $01  3232 pixels file icon (PNG only)
         </li>
         <li>
          $02  Other file icon
         </li>
         <li>
          $03  Cover (front)
         </li>
         <li>
          $04  Cover (back)
         </li>
         <li>
          $05  Leaflet page
         </li>
         <li>
          $06  Media (e.g. label side of CD)
         </li>
         <li>
          $07  Lead artist/lead performer/soloist
         </li>
         <li>
          $08  Artist/performer
         </li>
         <li>
          $09  Conductor
         </li>
         <li>
          $0A  Band/Orchestra
         </li>
         <li>
          $0B  Composer
         </li>
         <li>
          $0C  Lyricist/text writer
         </li>
         <li>
          $0D  Recording Location
         </li>
         <li>
          $0E  During recording
         </li>
         <li>
          $0F  During performance
         </li>
         <li>
          $10  Movie/video screen capture
         </li>
         <li>
          $11  A bright coloured fish
         </li>
         <li>
          $12  Illustration
         </li>
         <li>
          $13  Band/artist logotype
         </li>
         <li>
          $14  Publisher/Studio logotype
         </li>
        </ul>
        <div style="float: left; margin: 0px 10px 10px 0px;">
         <script async="" src="//pagead2.googlesyndication.com/pagead/js/adsbygoogle.js">
         </script>
         <br/>
         <br/>
         <ins class="adsbygoogle" data-ad-client="ca-pub-1156020804265294" data-ad-slot="8898497246" style="display:inline-block;width:336px;height:280px">
         </ins>
         <br/>
         <script>
          (adsbygoogle=window.adsbygoogle||[]).push({});
         </script>
        </div>
        <p>
         Quite an exhaustive list, and while a single MP3 file could embed all of the above images, in practice only
         <strong>
          one image
         </strong>
         is ever usually embedded.
        </p>
        <h2>
         File Sizes
        </h2>
        <p>
         Unfortunately, any additional information that you add to an MP3 file will
         <strong>
          increase
         </strong>
         its file size and this is of particular importance when adding images due to their potential size, even with compressed images such as JPEGs.
        </p>
        <p>
         However, this does need to be taken in context. For example, adding an 80kB JPEG image to a single 8MB podcast wont have a significant effect; its only a
         <strong>
          1%
         </strong>
         increase in file size.
        </p>
        <p>
         If on the other hand you add an 80kB album image to every single track in your MP3 collection, lets say of 1,000 songs, then youll need any additional 80MB of storage, which could otherwise hold a further 20 songs or so (another 2 albums).
        </p>
        <h2>
         Current Media Player Support
        </h2>
        <p>
         <strong>
          <a href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/wp-content/uploads/2008/06/mona200.jpg">
           <img align="right" alt="How to add Cover artwork to an MP3" border="0" height="200" src="http://www.richardfarrar.com/wp-content/uploads/2008/06/mona200-thumb.jpg" style="margin: 5px 0px 5px 15px; border: 0px none;" width="200"/>
          </a>
          Windows Media Player
         </strong>
         embeds
         <em>
          album artwork
         </em>
         as 200 x 200 pixel images, although will display larger images if they are embedded in the playing file as a larger size.
         <strong>
          iTunes
         </strong>
         currently displays
         <em>
          album art
         </em>
         as 200 x 200 pixel images. The picture to the right is sized at
         <strong>
          200 x 200
         </strong>
         pixels by way of example and is
         <strong>
          35kB
         </strong>
         in file size.
        </p>
        <p>
         The resolution of the
         <strong>
          iPod nano
         </strong>
         and
         <strong>
          iPod classic
         </strong>
         screens is 320 x 240 pixels. The
         <strong>
          iPod touch
         </strong>
         screen is 480 x 320 pixels, more than sufficient to display images of 200 x 200 pixels.
        </p>
        <h2>
         The Current Standard
        </h2>
        <p>
         <a href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/wp-content/uploads/2008/06/mona300.jpg">
          <img align="right" alt="Mona Lisa 300 x 300 pixels cover art added to an mp3" border="0" height="300" src="http://www.richardfarrar.com/wp-content/uploads/2008/06/mona300-thumb.jpg" style="margin: 5px 0px 0px 15px; border: 0px none;" width="300"/>
         </a>
         The majority of podcasts that include images embedded within them adopt an image size of 300 x 300 pixels.
        </p>
        <p>
         The picture to the right is sized at
         <strong>
          300 x 300
         </strong>
         pixels and is
         <strong>
          62kB
         </strong>
         in file size by way of example.
        </p>
        <p>
         JPEG images of these dimensions will vary in file size (dependant on the compression ratio used and image complexity) from around 10kB to 80kB or so. A 300 x 300 pixel image is actually over twice the size of a 200 x 200 image, and will consequently lead to approximately double file sizes.
        </p>
        <h2>
         Adding Your Own Pictures
        </h2>
        <p>
         So if youre producing your own podcast and want to enhance it with your own logo, or just want to embellish some of the tracks that you already have in your MP3 collection with album art, whats the best way forward?
        </p>
        <p>
         Its probably best to standardise on
         <strong>
          JPEG
         </strong>
         images to ensure that your artwork can be seen on the majority of possible playback devices.
        </p>
        <p>
         Image sizes are probably best set at
         <strong>
          300 x 300 pixels
         </strong>
         to display in reasonable quality on most playback systems. However, if youre concerned about the space taken up by these images, 200 x 200 pixel images may be the better option for you, reducing the image file size to about half that of a 300 x 300 pixel image. The
         <a href="http://www.bbc.co.uk/" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-article', 'http://www.bbc.co.uk/', 'BBC');" target="_blank">
          BBC
         </a>
         (a useful technical yardstick Ive always found) embed 300 x 300 images in their podcasts.
        </p>
        <p>
         If your current software doesnt allow you to embed or add images to your MP3 files directly, then standalone
         <strong>
          tag editing software
         </strong>
         should offer you this functionality. Some useful examples of such are:
        </p>
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="http://easytag.sourceforge.net/" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-article', 'http://easytag.sourceforge.net/', 'EasyTAG');">
           EasyTAG
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="http://filerename.co.uk/" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-article', 'http://filerename.co.uk/', 'Filerename.co.uk');">
           Filerename.co.uk
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="http://www.jthink.net/jaikoz/" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-article', 'http://www.jthink.net/jaikoz/', 'Jaikoz');">
           Jaikoz
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="http://www.mp3tag.de/en/" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-article', 'http://www.mp3tag.de/en/', 'Mp3tag');">
           Mp3tag
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="http://www.tagtuner.com/" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-article', 'http://www.tagtuner.com/', 'TagTuner');">
           TagTuner
          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="http://www.softpointer.com/tr.htm" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-article', 'http://www.softpointer.com/tr.htm', 'Tag&amp;Rename');" target="_blank">
           Tag&amp;Rename
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </div>

          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
           <p>
            Ive been looling into metadata a bit recently.
           </p>
           <p>
            The phrase album art isnt strictly speaking correct when referring to single track mp3 files.
           </p>
           <p>
            iTunes stores artwork in the music file and as such is actually track artwork, whereas windows media player stores the artwork for the album in its own library database, and as a separate file in the album directory  so that can be called album artwork.
           </p>
           <p>
            If youre only interested in adding album artwork, then utilities like album art aggregator are very useful.  It uses the artist and album data to find artwork on amazon.com.
           </p>
          </div>

          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
           <p>
            <b>
             @Luk:
            </b>
            Im not immediately aware of any software that will do what you want, but it may be worth trawling through the web to see. Alternatively, depending on your technical prowess, you could write a script to copy files only if the source MP3 contains an embedded image ID3 tag.
           </p>

           <p>
            What I found is that there are devices that will not display artwork larger than 200200.   For example, I spent days trying to figure out why some art would display and others not on my new DLink DSM-520 Media Player.  After trial and error, I confirmed that 200200 is the maximum size that would display on that device.  I also like Mp3tag to edit tags.  It works well.
           </p>

           </p>
           <p>
            I use an old paint program (Paint shop pro 7). It loads in a flash and within a few clicks you can have your image resized.
           </p>
           <p>
            300300 is fine for most of todays devices. So I simply find the image then load it up, if I have nothing better to do Ill maybe jazz it up a bit, save it as folder.jpg in My Documents.
           </p>
           <p>
            Then load up your tagging software and import the image. You can then save the next file over the old one for quick and easy access.
           </p>
           <p>
            If the artwork is embedded in the actual MP3s themselves then most devices will show the artwork with no problems.
           </p>
           <p>
            If you get everything setup first time round hopefully your never need to do anything with your files again, well, thats the way I look at it!
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="comment-reply">

            Reply
           </a>
          </div>
         </article>
        </li>

              However, is your artwork actually being
              <em>
               embedded
              </em>
              in the tracks, as often album artwork for a collection of album tracks is actually saved in the album folder as a separate JPEG image and not embedded separately in each album track?
             </p>

             </p>

            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              <strong>
               @abel:
              </strong>
              Artwork hidden in MP3 files is embedded using ID3 tags as described in the post above. If you want to do the same with tracks ripped from your own CDs, youll need to use a tag editor to add the artwork to the MP3 files.
             </p>
             <p>
              Alternatively you could use different ripping software that would rip your tracks and add the artwork at the same time, like
              <a href="http://www.mediamonkey.com/" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://www.mediamonkey.com/', 'MediaMonkey');" rel="nofollow">
               MediaMonkey
              </a>
              for example.
             </p>
            </div>

         <article itemprop="comment" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/UserComments">

                08 Dec 09 at 2:45 pm
               </a>
              </time>
             </p>
            </header>
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              I use
              <strong>
               72 dpi
              </strong>
              resolution, which seems to be a fairly standard resolution for web/computer based images.
             </p>
             <p>
              Regarding the JPEG quality, thats probably a bit more subjective as lower quality will lead to smaller file sizes, but will obviously lead to poorer images, which can be in the eye of the beholder. Maybe a bit of experimentation is required;  trying a few different settings to find a quality level that you find acceptable without too many visual artefacts.
             </p>
            </div>

            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              Hi, a very good question, but unfortunately the answer isnt simple as it really depends how your MP3 player has implemented the ID3 specification.
             </p>
             <p>
              My post on
              <strong>
               <a href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/alternative-id3-tags-for-adding-artwork-to-mp3-files/" rel="nofollow">
                Alternative ID3 Tags for Adding Artwork to MP3 Files
               </a>
              </strong>
              should explain things for you however.
             </p>
             <p>
              I would certainly counsel against putting artwork in every track as this would, as you say, take up a huge amount of unnecessary space.
             </p>
            </div>

            I hate MP3.
           </p>
           <p>
            A few years ago, I added cover art to ALL my mp3 files using iTunes. Now after I installed Win7 with WMP, I no longer use iTunes. Unfortunetely, WMP cannot read the cover art from all mp3 files  only som of them.
           </p>
           <p>
            If I add album art to an album in WMP, it refuses to add the cover to all files in the album. Nomatter how I do it. Likewise, Windows Explorer can read the album art for the album, but not all files in the album.
           </p>
           <p>
            What is wrong with people making software for playing mp3 files? I mean, this is not getting a rocket to the moon or something. How hard can it be?
           </p>
           <p>

               <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/#comment-774" itemprop="url">
                27 Jan 10 at 6:30 pm
               </a>
              </time>
             </p>
            </header>
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              Like you say, Im not familiar with iTunes, but it does seem to suggest that the artwork has been embedded in the files, although its always possible that the artwork could be saved in the album folder with the tracks associated to the particular album.
             </p>
             <p>
              You could always use a free tool like
              <strong>
               <a href="http://www.mp3tag.de/en/" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://www.mp3tag.de/en/', 'mp3tag');" rel="nofollow">
                mp3tag
               </a>
              </strong>
              , which will show you all the additional data actually embedded in the tracks themselves. That way youll be certain and be able to see whats actually happening for yourself.
             </p>
            </div>
            <div class="comment-reply">
             <a aria-label="Reply to Richard" class="comment-reply-link" href="/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/?replytocom=774#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-774", "774", "respond", "55" )'>

           <p>
            For the art to show in windows explorer you will need to place a folder.jpg in the folder. Then when you look at the folders in thumbnail view it will replace the standard yellow folder with whatever the folder.jpg file is.
           </p>

          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
           <p>
            Hi, thank you for the replies. Ive tried ID3-TagIT (my tag editor of first choice), mptagger, winamp, foobar2k, id3kill, media monkey, and a couple of others whose names escape me at the moment. I do have tag&amp;rename, although I havent used it in a while but will dig it out and see what it can do.
           </p>
           <p>
            Ive also checked to be sure theres not an external album art jpg somewhere that these are referring back to. My best guess at the moment after digging into this some more is that the problem files seem to use the id3v2.4 format, and perhaps tag editors that expect to see a v2.3 tag are unable to remove the picture, even when they say the tag has been completely removed. Im going to explore this angle in more depth.
           </p>
           <p>
            Richard, I appreciate your offer to take a look at one of the tracks, and Ill be glad to send you a copy of the next one I encounter. (Ive deleted the originals of the last batch I fixed by converting  and I agree, this is a solution to be avoided if at all possible.) Im certain that Ill run into others shortly, though.
           </p>
           <p>
            Thanks again for your help.
           </p>

           <p class="comment-meta">
            <time class="comment-time" datetime="2010-05-10T00:12:57+00:00" itemprop="commentTime">
             <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/#comment-978" itemprop="url">
              10 May 10 at 12:12 am
             </a>
            </time>
           </p>
          </header>
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
           <p>
            Mystery solved  I think.
           </p>
           <p>
            When I first opened the files with Id3TagIT, it showed that a v1 and a v2.3 tag were present. I removed both of them (it reported no tags of any kind at this point), and closed the program. However, the pictures were still present in the mp3, as shown by ACDSee (which displays any image in any file). Looking at these files with various tag editors, there were no apparent tags present at all in the files  yet still the embedded pictures.
           </p>
           <p>
            It wasnt until I accidentally opened the problem files a
            <em>
             second
            </em>
            time in Id3TagIT that it reported a v2.4 tag was present! I removed this 2.4 tag and presto! the images were gone. Im not sure if there were both versions present originally (is that even possible?) and the v2.3 masked the v2.4, or what. Also not sure why any of the other tag editors failed to spot the 2.4 tag. But no matter, Im good now. Just thought Id mention it in case anyone else ever has the same problem. If you dont succeed the first time, try again.
            <img alt=":-)" class="wp-smiley" src="http://www.richardfarrar.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;"/>
           </p>
          </div>

            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              Hi Luke, Unless you are really struggling with storage on your system, Im not sure its worth the effort (if indeed its at all possible) as the storage requirement for the artwork is fractional compared to the music itself.
             </p>
             <p>
              Windows Media Player stores artwork per album, which is much more efficient than storing the same artwork for every track. Im not sure if you can stop this behaviour in Media Player, I suspect that its deeply embedded within the inner workings of the software.
             </p>
            </div>
            <div class="comment-reply">
             <a aria-label="Reply to Richard" class="comment-reply-link" href="/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/?replytocom=1053#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-1053", "1053", "respond", "55" )'>
              Reply
             </a>
            </div>
           </article>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </li>

              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.php.net/manual/en/refs.utilspec.audio.php" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://www.php.net/manual/en/refs.utilspec.audio.php', 'http://www.php.net/manual/en/refs.utilspec.audio.php');" rel="nofollow">

              </a>
              .

            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              For phones I think 300300 is a good size, but I use bigger sizes because I use the same mp3 files in my PC and in my phone, in my PC I prefer big album arts.
             </p>
             <p>
              BUT, I realized that album art (embedded directly into the mp3) bigger than 600600 pixels dont show up in Nokia phones music players, so now I use a maximun 600600 in all files and it shows up perfectly in my PC/Winamp and in my phone music player. My phone is a Nokia 5320, but I think this is the same for all the Nokia phones with Symbian OS/S60 system, which is the system of my phone. I hope this help you.
             </p>
             <p>
              I use Mp3Tag for tag editing and album art embedding and never had a problem, I strongly recommend this powerful tag editor, works perfect and you never have surprices.
             </p>
             <p>
              (PS: sorry for my english)
             </p>
            </div>

           <p>
            I found this (
            <a href="http://blog.lostpaperclips.com/2010/10/16/embedding-images-in-mp3-files-redux" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://blog.lostpaperclips.com/2010/10/16/embedding-images-in-mp3-files-redux', 'http://blog.lostpaperclips.com/2010/10/16/embedding-images-in-mp3-files-redux');" rel="nofollow">
             http://blog.lostpaperclips.com/2010/10/16/embedding-images-in-mp3-files-redux
            </a>
            ) useful. Perhaps not so helpful for those not on Linux, but this let me put artwork into all my MP3s so that I could see them on my Android phone.
           </p>
          </div>

            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              Hi,
             </p>
             <p>
              Unfortunately not. WAV files dont really support metadata as such, although some flavours of WAV such as the
              <strong>
               Broadcast Wave Format
              </strong>
              (BWF) do support some limited metadata, but aimed more at the broadcasting industry and not consumer oriented stuff such as album art.
             </p>
            </div>
            <div class="comment-reply">

          </div>

            <header class="comment-header">
             <p class="comment-author" itemprop="creator" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
              <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/45ead74d582834e83e4b476b7fce992b?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/45ead74d582834e83e4b476b7fce992b?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="48"/>
              <span itemprop="name">
               <a class="comment-author-link" href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/" itemprop="url" rel="external nofollow">
                Richard
               </a>
              </span>
              <span class="says">
               commented
              </span>
             </p>
             <p class="comment-meta">
              <time class="comment-time" datetime="2010-12-21T17:26:36+00:00" itemprop="commentTime">
               <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/#comment-2872" itemprop="url">
                21 Dec 10 at 5:26 pm
               </a>
              </time>
             </p>
            </header>
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              When using Windows Media Player, album art is saved as an image in the folder with the rest of the album tracks and not actually in the track itself, so if you copy an individual track to another device such as a mobile phone, the album art probably isnt getting copied across as well. If you copied the whole album folder across, then the album art may work.
             </p>
             <p>
              It is possible to embed album art into individual WMA tracks using something like the MP3TAG editor, but youd have to do this on each track individually.
             </p>
            </div>
            <div class="comment-reply">

            You can use Winamp to link a mp3 file to a specific jpg album art without embedded it. Definitely, there are some disadvantages if you want to move your music to other devices or share it via internet.

            <br/>
            <a href="http://www.withsteps.com/602/include-album-art-into-mp3-files.html" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://www.withsteps.com/602/include-album-art-into-mp3-files.html', 'http://www.withsteps.com/602/include-album-art-into-mp3-files.html');" rel="nofollow">

        <li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1" id="comment-2924">
         <article itemprop="comment" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/UserComments">
          <header class="comment-header">
           <p class="comment-author" itemprop="creator" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
            <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/fa96f1db1ca6968f571e7069701e12ed?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/fa96f1db1ca6968f571e7069701e12ed?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="48"/>
            <span itemprop="name">
             Phil
            </span>
            <span class="says">
             commented
            </span>
           </p>
           <p class="comment-meta">
            <time class="comment-time" datetime="2011-01-25T20:12:38+00:00" itemprop="commentTime">
             <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/#comment-2924" itemprop="url">
              25 Jan 11 at 8:12 pm
             </a>
            </time>
           </p>
          </header>
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
           <p>
            Ive been very interested to read some of the reviews/comments regarding embedding artwork in mp3s. I have both a comment and a question.
           </p>
           <p>
            Firstly, as I understand it, neither WMP nor Winamp actually embed artwork, they simply create an image file in the mp3 folder and refer to it when the music is played. (This is why artwork will often not appear if you move the music file to another location). WMP creates a (hidden) file called AlbumArtLarge.jpg and Winamp creates a file called .jpg. There are advantages and disadvantages with both methods, depending on how you listen to your music.
           </p>
           <p>
            On the other hand, some music files do actually have artwork embedded, usually while being ripped to your computer. This way the picture will always (or almost always) appear when the music is played. Ive got such a file on my computer right now and it is this file which brings me to my question. The mp3 has been tagged incorrectly (by my music ripper, not by me). I edited the tags so that the track would match the others in the folder and now the embedded artwork no longer shows up! Yes, I could just rerip my CD, but Id rather learn whats happened and how to rectify it.
           </p>
           <p>
            Right-clicking the file in XP lets me see some limited ID3 information. Viewing the file information in Winamp (my player of choice) shows me both ID3 and ID3v2 tags. However, Winamp does not store image metadata in the ID3v2 tag, it uses a different method (as described above), which means that reattaching the artwork results in a new jpg file being created.
           </p>
           <p>
            The file was originally encoded in iTunes (before I abandoned it with an all-consuming hatred of all things Apple) and I have to assume this is where the artwork was originally embedded. Id like to know how this was done and if it can be reproduced (without using iTunes). Id be interested to read your suggestions.
           </p>
          </div>

            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              Hi Phil, It looks like you have got a pretty good understanding of whats going on. The problem might be with your troublesome file that there are actually
              <a href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/alternative-id3-tags-for-adding-artwork-to-mp3-files/" rel="nofollow">
               20 tags that can store album art in an MP3
              </a>
              and unfortunately most software will only display one of them. Try using MP3Tag, or a similar tag editor to look at all of these artwork tags to see if you can track down the errant artwork.
             </p>
            </div>

            <header class="comment-header">

              <time class="comment-time" datetime="2011-03-08T15:31:40+00:00" itemprop="commentTime">
               <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/#comment-2956" itemprop="url">
                08 Mar 11 at 3:31 pm
               </a>
              </time>
             </p>
            </header>
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              Hi,
             </p>
             <p>
              Thanks for your kind comments. Regarding your question, the ID3 tagging standard for album art in MP3s doesnt specify a size, you can put in whatever image size you want. I think iTunes uses 200x200px images, but as I dont use iTunes I cant verify this; they may also have changed things as display sizes are increasing with devices like the iPad.
             </p>
            </div>

            <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/ff79ab53e4fcbe6fc6a1e365cb2369d3?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/ff79ab53e4fcbe6fc6a1e365cb2369d3?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="48"/>

           <p class="comment-meta">
            <time class="comment-time" datetime="2011-03-16T02:14:38+00:00" itemprop="commentTime">
             <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/#comment-2979" itemprop="url">
              16 Mar 11 at 2:14 am
             </a>
            </time>
           </p>
          </header>
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
           <p>
            I have an MP3 of an obscure musical group for which Windows Media Player couldnt find any album info.  I like to have the album cover showing when a song is playing, so I found a jpeg image of the cover online and copied it to my computer.  Then I discovered a way to link it to my mp3 through WMP.  If I right-click on the mp3 in the library tab, choose advanced tag editor, click pictures, and click add, I am able to add the picture to the mp3 file and have it display in WMP.  I thought this information might help others with simple needs like mine.
           </p>
          </div>

            </header>
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              Hi, If youve burnt a CD that can be played on standard CD players, the the audio files would be converted to WAV files that dont support embedded artwork unfortunately. The only way would be to burn a DATA CD with MP3 files and their associated embedded artwork, which might play on more modern CD players, but wouldnt be classed as a standard CD.
             </p>
            </div>
            <div class="comment-reply">

             <p class="comment-meta">
              <time class="comment-time" datetime="2011-06-01T15:26:45+00:00" itemprop="commentTime">
               <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/#comment-3056" itemprop="url">
                01 Jun 11 at 3:26 pm
               </a>
              </time>
             </p>
            </header>
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              Hi, Without having direct experience of your phone its difficult to tell. Maybe working backwards would help. If you have an MP3 that displays the artwork correctly on your phone, download that file onto your PC and analyze the artwork in MP3TAG to see what size it is, what file type (e.g. jpeg) and which artwork id it uses (there are numerous
              <a href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/alternative-id3-tags-for-adding-artwork-to-mp3-files/" rel="nofollow">
               different possibilities
              </a>
              ). Then try and use these same settings when you upload new tracks to your phone to see if it works.
             </p>
             <p>
              Good luck.
             </p>
            </div>

          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
           <p>
            Regarding Embedded Image Size
            <br/>
            I have noticed that when saving JPG files in Photoshop, a higher compression results in a much smaller file size. Considering this, is there anything wrong with embedding a JPG with 500 x 500 pixel size? Since Windows Media Player has the feature to show the album art in a big window, this size allows more detail to show especially helpful when there is a lot of small text on the album cover.
            <br/>
            BTWI use MP3 Tag Assistant Pro 2.9.2 program which makes it easy to embed all songs in an album in one step.
            <br/>
            Would appreciate your feedback and thank you in advance.
           </p>
          </div>

             <p class="comment-meta">
              <time class="comment-time" datetime="2011-07-11T12:25:53+00:00" itemprop="commentTime">
               <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/#comment-3098" itemprop="url">
                11 Jul 11 at 12:25 pm
               </a>
              </time>
             </p>
            </header>
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              Your logic is perfectly correct, but if you compress an image too much you will begin to see compression artefacts and loose quality, so youll need to experiment to find the best compression settings that work for you balancing quality against filesize. Having said that theres absolutely no reason not to go for 500x500px images if it works for you.
             </p>
            </div>

          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
           <p>
            Hi. I need to be enlightened! Im a MAC user at this time. The cover art of all my iTunes audio files appears in iTunes and on my IPOD. However, when I connect my IPOD to my multimedia car system which also displays cover art, only some of the cover art appears. It doesnt seem to have anything to do with the audio type, as aac, mp3 and m4a all have this problem. On one song, the cover art appears and then on the next which is the exact same format, it does not. I tried embedding the cover art with the Apple Script, but this didnt do the trick either.I also tried replacing the artwork with smaller or bigger sized pics, but to no avail. Another thing I noticed, when I go into Artwork and manually erase the cover art on the file, sometimes, another one pops up on the iTunes screen  (from who knows where..) but it is not visible in the Artwork box.. Do you have any miracle solution to this problem ??
            <img alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" src="http://www.richardfarrar.com/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;"/>
            Thanks

          <li class="comment even depth-2" id="comment-3136">
           <article itemprop="comment" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/UserComments">
            <header class="comment-header">
             <p class="comment-author" itemprop="creator" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
              <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" src="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/2b2281c4e5d5c92be7d81821545c706a?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/2b2281c4e5d5c92be7d81821545c706a?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="48"/>
              <span itemprop="name">
               Marc
              </span>
              <span class="says">
               commented
              </span>
             </p>
             <p class="comment-meta">
              <time class="comment-time" datetime="2011-08-15T17:21:25+00:00" itemprop="commentTime">
               <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/#comment-3136" itemprop="url">
                15 Aug 11 at 5:21 pm
               </a>
              </time>
             </p>
            </header>
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              Hi Nicole, being a Mac user I suppose you stumbled across am iTunes specific handling of artwork. In fact, iTunes does not automatically store the artwork in the music-files but the artwork will be stored separately on your file system in a folder called Album Artwork which resides in your Music/iTunes folder. iTunes can handle both, integrated artwork in the music files as well as of course its own separate storage scheme. But alternative non-apple players are usually not aware of the apple scheme and hence only show the artwork for the files which embed the artwork. You will most likely have a mixture of both depending of the source of your files.
              <br/>
              There is help, of course, there are several programs out which will transfer the external apple storage scheme to the internal one, e.g., have a look at Dougs scripts here:
              <a href="http://dougscripts.com/itunes/scripts/ss.php?sp=embedart" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://dougscripts.com/itunes/scripts/ss.php?sp=embedart', 'http://dougscripts.com/itunes/scripts/ss.php?sp=embedart');" rel="nofollow">
               http://dougscripts.com/itunes/scripts/ss.php?sp=embedart
              </a>
             </p>
             <p>
              best
             </p>
            </div>

             <p>
              Hi Dan, Yes it certainly can co-exist with the album cover. This is something I actually covered in a separate article that you may be interested in reading:
              <br/>
              <a href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/alternative-id3-tags-for-adding-artwork-to-mp3-files/" rel="nofollow">
               http://www.richardfarrar.com/alternative-id3-tags-for-adding-artwork-to-mp3-files/
              </a>
              <br/>
              The program that I use for editing a tracks ID3 tags (
              <a href="http://www.mp3tag.de/en/" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://www.mp3tag.de/en/', 'MP3TAG');" rel="nofollow">
               MP3TAG
              </a>
              ) can definitely allow you to add multiple images to an MP3 file, but Im sure there are many other tag editing programs that would work in a similar fashion.
             </p>

            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              Hi, If the id3.jar class defaults to extracting only a single image from one of its inbuilt functions, you may have to use one of the classes lower level functions to extract all of the ID3 source data and then extract the separate images yourself, referring to the ID3 specification for the specific storage and encoding mechanisms. It should be possible, but may take a little extra effort on your part unfortunately.
             </p>
            </div>

          </header>
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
           <p>
            Nice info. I have to add that iTunes can add atwork too.
           </p>
           <p>
            Find the album you want to add artwork to
            <br/>
            Select all the tracks in the album you want to add the iTunes artwork to the ID3 tag
            <br/>
            In the bottom left-hand corner click on show/hide artwork
            <br/>
            Right-click on the artwork image that is displayed and select copy
            <br/>
            Now right-click on the tracks youve highlighted and select Get info
            <br/>
            In the pop-up box that right-click in the artwork field and select paste
           </p>
           <p>
            source:
            <a href="http://www.onetipaday.com/2006/12/31/how-to-add-itunes-artwork-to-mp3-id3-tags-using-itunes/" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://www.onetipaday.com/2006/12/31/how-to-add-itunes-artwork-to-mp3-id3-tags-using-itunes/', 'http://www.onetipaday.com/2006/12/31/how-to-add-itunes-artwork-to-mp3-id3-tags-using-itunes/');" rel="nofollow">
             http://www.onetipaday.com/2006/12/31/how-to-add-itunes-artwork-to-mp3-id3-tags-using-itunes/
            </a>
           </p>
          </div>
          <div class="comment-reply">

              <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
               <p>
                I can confirm that MP3tag does actually embed the artwork and, therefore, the art transfers to a portable media player.  My congratulations to the German designers.  Only seems to work when copying and pasting rather than loading artwork (where it creates a link rather than embedding), but I can live with that.  Aspect ratio is my next problem, but I think that is to do with a square art image (an LP cover) trying to display on a rectangular PMP screen.
               </p>
              </div>

            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              Hi Jeff, That sounds like quite a task you have set yourself! I would say that
              <strong>
               if
              </strong>
              you have the artwork
              <strong>
               embedded
              </strong>
              in the audio files then the remaining JPG
              <em>
               should
              </em>
              be superfluous. However, to be on the safe side I would do a test run first to make sure that youre not going to loose any potentially irreplaceable artwork. Another thing maybe to consider for an album where the JPG isnt a separate file is that you might need the artwork to be embedded in every track on the album to be on the safe side, although this involves an inevitable bit of duplication.
             </p>
             <p>
              For mass artwork and audio management, have you considered something like
              <a href="http://www.blisshq.com/index.html" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://www.blisshq.com/index.html', 'bliss');" rel="nofollow">
               bliss
              </a>
              ?
             </p>

          <header class="comment-header">

            <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" src="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/c306bbfdb398beb59421fe02c764c86f?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/c306bbfdb398beb59421fe02c764c86f?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="48"/>

           <p class="comment-meta">
            <time class="comment-time" datetime="2011-09-28T04:16:17+00:00" itemprop="commentTime">
             <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/#comment-3196" itemprop="url">
              28 Sep 11 at 4:16 am
             </a>
            </time>
           </p>
          </header>
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
           <p>
            Im just going through a reorganization of my own music library. Im normally using iTunes on the PC for playback. Album artwork downloaded through iTunes is 600600, and that is what I then paste into the individual files. This might be a bit excessive in space, but MP3 encoding quality has increased as well and files have become bigger due to that fact, and 600600 is a good compromise for seeing details like text on the album cover.
           </p>
           <p>
            When you use Get Info on a iTunes song it isnt clear where the artwork shown is coming from, but if you have an Explorer folder open in Large Icons mode, you can see if the MP3 files actually contain the art. If necessary, I then use copy from the Get Info artwork page of one of the albums song files, then multi-select all files of the album and use Get Info again which then shows an empty artwork field where I paste the image. You then see iTunes working on updating the ID3 tags of all files and can also control the result by looking at the open album folder in Explorer. Of course this also works for adding art from a non-iTunes source like a scan or website, just use e.g. Copy Image in Firefox, then paste it into the artwork field.
           </p>
           <p>
            As another test if the embedding was successful, you can run the song with Windows Media Player and check if the album art is displayed as background.
           </p>
           <p>
            It is interesting that the standard supports a whole list of images, this might be useful one day for having a complete jewel case with CD simulated in a VR environment.
           </p>
          </div>

             <p class="comment-meta">
              <time class="comment-time" datetime="2011-10-01T16:56:58+00:00" itemprop="commentTime">
               <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/#comment-3202" itemprop="url">

               </a>
              </time>
             </p>
            </header>
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              Hi, Glad to hear that you found the article informative. MP3TAG actually embeds the album artwork at its original resolution, but your playback software or device (e.g. WMP) may not be displaying the full resolution of the artwork that is actually in the MP3 file. Try a test with MP3TAG and then play the file in something like
              <a href="http://www.videolan.org/vlc/" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://www.videolan.org/vlc/', 'VLC Player');" rel="nofollow">
               VLC Player
              </a>
              and you should see what I mean.
             </p>
            </div>
            <div class="comment-reply">
             <a aria-label="Reply to Richard" class="comment-reply-link" href="/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/?replytocom=3202#respond" onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-3202", "3202", "respond", "55" )'>
              Reply
             </a>
            </div>
           </article>

              <a href="http://www.mp3tag.de/en/" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://www.mp3tag.de/en/', 'MP3TAG');" rel="nofollow">
               MP3TAG
              </a>
              ) actually supports importing from
              <strong>
               Discogs
              </strong>
              :
             </p>

              <em>
               Import from Amazon, discogs, freedb, MusicBrainz Save typing and import tags from online databases like Amazon, discogs, freedb, MusicBrainz, and more.
              </em>
             </p>
             <p>
              Perhaps its worth giving this a try. For mass management, perhaps have a look at
              <a href="http://www.blisshq.com/feature-album-art.html" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://www.blisshq.com/feature-album-art.html', 'Bliss');" rel="nofollow">

              </a>
              , which also links to Discogs? Hope this helps a little.

           </p>

             <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/#comment-3886" itemprop="url">
              15 Jan 13 at 4:12 am
             </a>
            </time>
           </p>
          </header>
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
           <p>
            Seems to me that mp3  or some new variant  could be designed to contain say 3 or 4 photos as well as a duration setting for each photo. This would make it easy to create lyric slides for songs, avoiding the AVI file which is not only huge, but has much lower resolution than the art embedded in an mp3. For instance, the lyrics of a song can be sized to fit 4 slides at a half meg each. Add the mp3 and that totals only 5M. The same 4 slides and mp3 converted to AVI is 38M. Plus its fuzzy. Anybody know of any such thing or any such plan?
           </p>
          </div>

              <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
               <p>
                Thanks, Richard,
                <br/>
                If any soft engineer should see this and get ideas, to reduce file size, we dont need ways to adjust the photos or add text or art since that would be done before embedding. And we dont need transitions between slides because singers need to get to the next slide immediately. Besides, those cool transitions are annoying. Keep in mind, the slide should be 1024 x 768 pixels, not album cover size. This gives lots more room for the lyrics.
               </p>
              </div>

              <header class="comment-header">
               <p class="comment-author" itemprop="creator" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
                <img alt="" class="avatar avatar-48 photo" height="48" src="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/ad88a16a57b99feb47e92cb881c9767c?s=48&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g" srcset="http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/ad88a16a57b99feb47e92cb881c9767c?s=96&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x" width="48"/>

                 <a class="comment-author-link" href="http://pjsho.ws" itemprop="url" rel="external nofollow">
                  Joshua McGee
                 </a>
                </span>
                <span class="says">
                 commented
                </span>
               </p>
               <p class="comment-meta">
                <time class="comment-time" datetime="2014-04-15T19:58:50+00:00" itemprop="commentTime">
                 <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/#comment-4419" itemprop="url">
                  15 Apr 14 at 7:58 pm
                 </a>
                </time>
               </p>
              </header>
              <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
               <p>
                I settled on using
                <a href="http://eyed3.nicfit.net/" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://eyed3.nicfit.net/', 'eyeD3');" rel="nofollow">
                 eyeD3
                </a>
                for album artwork for the
                <a href="http://pjsho.ws" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://pjsho.ws', 'pjsho.ws');" rel="nofollow">
                 pjsho.ws
                </a>
                site, the reason being its command-line interface.  I created a template for album artwork, and as part of the concert packaging script that canonicalizes titles, adds a text file, packages and seeds torrent files, and so on, I generate an image file with an ImageMagick script and tag the tracks with this image using eyeD3.
               </p>
               <p>
                So my advice for anyone looking for a scriptable solution is
                <a href="http://eyed3.nicfit.net/" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://eyed3.nicfit.net/', 'eyeD3');" rel="nofollow">
                 eyeD3
                </a>
                .
               </p>
               <p>
                Thanks again for this post pointing me in the right direction!
               </p>
              </div>

            </time>

          </header>
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
           <p>
            Id discovered another auto cover art embedding tool, which Ive found to be quite useful. It is called Taghycardia. The free app tags mp3s automatically using online as well as local images whenever the latter exist, which speeds up the process a lot. In addition, it performs some analysis, e.g. spots folders with the tracks having varying embedded pictures so the user could choose which one he or she wishes to use for the whole album.
           </p>
          </div>

             <p class="comment-meta">
              <time class="comment-time" datetime="2013-02-12T19:36:53+00:00" itemprop="commentTime">
               <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/#comment-3958" itemprop="url">
                12 Feb 13 at 7:36 pm
               </a>
              </time>
             </p>
            </header>
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              VLC will display already embedded cover art and you can also use VLC to edit the MP3s ID3 tags by going to
              <strong>
               Tools -&gt; Media Information
              </strong>
              (Ctrl+I). If you Right-Click the VLC traffic cone logo in the
              <em>
               General tab
              </em>
              of the
              <em>
               Media Information window
              </em>
              you are given the option to Download cover art, but how effective this is and where it gets the artwork from I dont know.
             </p>
             <p>
              If you want more control, try a dedicated tagging program like Mp3tag.
             </p>
            </div>
            <div class="comment-reply">

            <time class="comment-time" datetime="2013-06-15T15:30:55+00:00" itemprop="commentTime">
             <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/#comment-4180" itemprop="url">
              15 Jun 13 at 3:30 pm
             </a>
            </time>
           </p>
          </header>
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
           <p>
            Heres a website where you can add/edit mp3 album art and other parameters.
            <br/>
            <a href="http://tagmp3.net" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://tagmp3.net', 'http://tagmp3.net');" rel="nofollow">
             http://tagmp3.net
            </a>
            <br/>
            You can simply upload desired mp3 file, put your image/album art, title, artist, comments etc, and it will get you the updated mp3 file.
           </p>
          </div>

            <a href="http://meka-mp3-album-artwork-tool.software.informer.com/" onclick="__gaTracker('send', 'event', 'outbound-comment', 'http://meka-mp3-album-artwork-tool.software.informer.com/', 'Meka MP3 Album Artwork Tool');" rel="nofollow">

            </a>
            this week. Its free, lightweight, simple and quick  perfect if youre just adding album art to your files. I highly recommend it.

            Hi Richard.
            <br/>
            Great post. Im definitely a newbie to all of this and found you piece extremely informative. Being none technical in this field Im wondering if you could help me with something. I see that there are a range of image tags available (I also find A bright coloured fish amusing) but there are two that I have a particular interest in: $03  Cover (front) and $08  Artist/performer. Given that I could embed different images in both instances, are you aware of any technical issue which would prevent a windows phone mp3 player app from reading and showing the cover image tag (for Albums) and the different artist/performer tag (for Artists). I have not come across any app that currently seems to do this but it would be useful when you have a various artist Album and alike.

              Hi Ray,
             </p>
             <p>
              Thanks for your comment and Im pleased that my post managed to help you a little.
             </p>
             <p>
              In answer to your question there shouldnt be any technical issues that prevent multiple cover art being displayed, but I havent seen any implementation of this myself, so I dont think many manufacturers or software developers seem to support this. I did discuss this in another article on 
              <a href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/alternative-id3-tags-for-adding-artwork-to-mp3-files/" rel="nofollow">
               Alternative ID3 Tags for Adding Artwork to MP3 Files
              </a>
               that actually had a test track with all images included that you could try out on different media players. Hope this helps.
             </p>

              20 Oct 14 at 7:10 pm
             </a>
            </time>
           </p>
          </header>
          <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
           <p>
            I use Tag &amp; Rename (by Softpointer), it really rocks! You can add images to multiple files and easily rename complete albums, edit more than one thing at once on one or multiple files! Even adding lyrics or renaming the files themself is no problem..
           </p>
           <p>
            My only question is, the 200200 is already an outdated size though not on Windows Media Player or Winamp as they show small images, but for example when used in my car stereo unit or my smartphone the art shown is VERY POOR quality! I upgraded them as much as possible, some have 500500 others even 15001500 and all sizes in between, but which is the maximum used nowadays on any device?
           </p>
           <p>
            The problem with Windows Media Player is when youve update your art covers to 500500, when you play the song one time it automaticly changes the album arts back to a poor 200200 so youll never get all your files done when you also listen to them through Windows Media Player. Winamp doesnt do this to your files though! The only thing is that your player will crash if you have a big playlist with lost of big size album art covers to your mp3 files.
           </p>
           <p>
            Does anyone know what is the minimum size to get the nicest quality on your (lets say) smartphone screen?
           </p>
          </div>

               <a class="comment-time-link" href="http://www.richardfarrar.com/embedding-album-art-in-mp3-files/#comment-4627" itemprop="url">
                20 Oct 14 at 8:10 pm
               </a>
              </time>
             </p>
            </header>
            <div class="comment-content" itemprop="commentText">
             <p>
              Thanks for your feedback, and as by now youve realized that this is a bit of a thorny area with no real resolution. I wrote this post a few years back and it could probably do with being updated to be honest.
             </p>
             <p>
              Nowadays, I would probably go for 600600 for music, but theres always a trade-off with file size too.
             </p>
             <p>
              Interestingly, for podcasts, Apple recommends Create your cover art, which must be in the JPEG or PNG file formats and in the RGB color space with a minimum size of 1400 x 1400 pixels and a maximum size of 2048 x 2048 pixels!
             </p>
            </div>
